href=\\\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.CC-BY-4.0\\\"\\u003eLICENSE.CC-BY-4.0\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MIT\\\"\\u003eLICENSE.MIT\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MulanOWL-BY-1.0\\\"\\u003eLICENSE.MulanOWL-BY-1.0\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MulanPSL-2.0\\\"\\u003eLICENSE.MulanPSL-2.0\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003cdetails\\u003e\\n\\u003csummary\\u003eReasoning behind the licensing decisions\\u003c/summary\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eNOTE: The author is not a lawyer, so take the analysis below with extra\\ncaution. The author believes much of the reasoning are correct however...\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe official LoongArch manuals are released by Loongson with all rights\\nreserved. So first of all, we believe \\u003cem\\u003ethis project is a fair use of the\\noriginal work\\u003c/em\\u003e because:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003col dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eThe data collected here is consistent with the reality, with all original\\ncontent clearly marked and explained. Hence the data tables as a whole\\npose no risk to compatibility across the ecosystem, and by extension,\\nLoongson's legal interests.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eWe, and likely any potential consumer of the project, work on and/or use\\nproject for personal and/or academic purposes.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eAnd even if the project is eventually being consumed for commercial uses,\\nno Loongson interest is damaged because of (1).\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eThere is not any alternative that we know of, that is simultaneously:\\n\\u003cul dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003enot being tied to any specific project (see below), and\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eeasy for machine consumption (the official manual is in PDF only, and\\nthe English translation is in AsciiDoc).\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ol\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThere are already several LoongArch instruction encoding tables in existence:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cul dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003ethe array defined in \\u003ccode\\u003eopcodes/loongarch-opc.c\\u003c/code\\u003e of Binutils,\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003ethe TableGen data files in LLVM,\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003ethe \\u003ccode\\u003edecodetree\\u003c/code\\u003e definitions in QEMU, and\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eother ad-hoc definitions in various adapted JIT projects.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThey are invariably hard to integrate in projects other the originating one,\\nso if one wants proper LoongArch machine code support in another project they\\nhappen to work on, they would have to either duplicate efforts or leverage\\nthe \\u003ccode\\u003eloongarch-opcodes\\u003c/code\\u003e project -- compared to just giving up and adding no\\nLoongArch support, existence of the \\u003ccode\\u003eloongarch-opcodes\\u003c/code\\u003e project actually\\n\\u003cem\\u003ebenefits\\u003c/em\\u003e Loongson.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eRegarding the copyright holder of the project, it's the contributor to this\\nproject, because of \\u003ca href=\\\"https://www.gov.cn/guoqing/2021-10/29/content_5647633.htm\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\\u003e《中华人民共和国著作权法》\\u003c/a\\u003e第十三条、第十四条;\\nthe Chinese copyright law applies because right now all contributors to\\nthe project are PRC citizens to our knowledge.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAs to why attribution is required for the data tables, instead of simply\\nbeing public domain: according to 《中华人民共和国著作权法》第十条,\\nthe right of attribution (署名权) is a moral right that cannot be waived.\\nSo even if \\u003ca href=\\\"https://creativecommons.org/publicdomain/zero/1.0/\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\\u003eCC0-1.0\\u003c/a\\u003e is\\napplied to the project, in effect it would largely just become CC-BY, and\\nwith the disadvantage of being harder for people to understand because the\\n\\\"fallback path\\\" in the license text must be taken.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAs to why the Mulan licenses are allowed as alternative license choices:\\nthis is because the author wanted to be extra safe regarding the licensing,\\nespecially in the PRC jurisdiction. After checking the Chinese and English\\ntexts of the Mulan licenses, the author decided there is little risk adding\\nthem to the multiple-licensing choices.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/details\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv class=\\\"markdown-heading\\\" dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ch2 tabindex=\\\"-1\\\" class=\\\"heading-element\\\" dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eModifications to upstream specs\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\u003ca id=\\\"user-content-modifications-to-upstream-specs\\\" class=\\\"anchor\\\" aria-label=\\\"Permalink: Modifications to upstream specs\\\" href=\\\"#modifications-to-upstream-specs\\\"\\u003e\\u003csvg data-component=\\\"Octicon\\\" class=\\\"octicon octicon-link\\\" viewBox=\\\"0 0 16 16\\\" version=\\\"1.1\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" aria-hidden=\\\"true\\\"\\u003e\\u003cpath d=\\\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 0 2.83Z\\\"\\u003e\\u003c/path\\u003e\\u003c/svg\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eSome instruction mnemonics are changed, some syntactic sugar are dropped:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cul dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003edbcl\\u003c/code\\u003e is renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003edbgcall\\u003c/code\\u003e, and \\u003ccode\\u003ehvcl\\u003c/code\\u003e to \\u003ccode\\u003ehypcall\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe reason why the shorter names are chosen is unclear, but \\u003ccode\\u003esyscall\\u003c/code\\u003e remains\\nunchanged so the change actually made the naming inconsistent.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003eb[lt,ge][u]\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003eb[gt,le][u]\\u003c/code\\u003e with corresponding operand order swapped.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAll other two-register instructions have the operand in \\u003ccode\\u003erd, rj\\u003c/code\\u003e order, except\\nthese jump instructions. To preserve semantics the names have to be tweaked\\naccordingly. Also all other instructions with comparison semantics adopt the\\n\\u003ccode\\u003egt/le\\u003c/code\\u003e distinction, such as the boundary checks, so \\u003ccode\\u003elt/ge\\u003c/code\\u003e is not consistent\\neither.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003eertn\\u003c/code\\u003e is renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003eeret\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eNot using \\u003ccode\\u003eret\\u003c/code\\u003e for \\\"return\\\" is hard to understand, personally I think it's\\nbetter to stick with widely accepted naming conventions.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003einvtlb\\u003c/code\\u003e is renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003etlbinv\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAll TLB manipulation instructions start with \\u003ccode\\u003etlb\\u003c/code\\u003e except this one.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003ecsrrd\\u003c/code\\u003e, \\u003ccode\\u003ecsrwr\\u003c/code\\u003e, \\u003ccode\\u003egcsrrd\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003egcsrwr\\u003c/code\\u003e are removed.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe \\u003ccode\\u003ecsrrd\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003ecsrwr\\u003c/code\\u003e instructions can, to some degree, be seen as special\\ncases or \\\"specializations\\\" of \\u003ccode\\u003ecsrxchg\\u003c/code\\u003e, so remove these in favor of\\nnon-overlapping encodings. \\u003ccode\\u003egcsrrd\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003egcsrwr\\u003c/code\\u003e are similar.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe FCSR operands of\\u003ccode\\u003emovfcsr2gr\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003emovgr2fcsr\\u003c/code\\u003e are marked unsigned\\nimmediates instead of registers; the mnemonics are renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003efcsrrd\\u003c/code\\u003e and\\n\\u003ccode\\u003efcsrwr\\u003c/code\\u003e as well.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe FCSR is more like a configuration word than real register in terms of\\nexpected usage; but the manual and vendor toolchain all treat the slot as\\nan integer register, which is obviously wrong. Instruction naming is\\nadjusted accordingly (to make the FCSR more resemble CSR).\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eInstructions that operate on FCCs have the \\u003ccode\\u003ecf\\u003c/code\\u003e part renamed to \\u003ccode\\u003efcc\\u003c/code\\u003e in\\ntheir mnemonics.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eOther parts of the manual, especially the register names, refer to the bank\\nof 1-bit FP predicates as \\u003ccode\\u003efcc\\u003c/code\\u003e, but mnemonics have \\u003ccode\\u003ecf\\u003c/code\\u003e, which is\\ninconsistent.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eNaming symmetry is restored for several LBT instructions.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe x86 and ARM translation assists are almost always named \\u003ccode\\u003ex86foo\\u003c/code\\u003e and\\n\\u003ccode\\u003earmfoo\\u003c/code\\u003e respectively, but annoyingly some are named \\u003ccode\\u003esetx86foo\\u003c/code\\u003e and\\n\\u003ccode\\u003esetarmfoo\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e(After \\u003ca href=\\\"https://sourceware.org/pipermail/binutils/2023-June/128100.html\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\\u003ethe issue was reported\\u003c/a\\u003e\\nI received private confirmation that the names will not be amended but no\\njustification was given; I suppose it was because the \\u003ccode\\u003eset{x86,arm}foo\\u003c/code\\u003e ops\\nare not touching the actual LBT \\\"arch\\\" state, but I'm not sure, and here the\\nadjusted names are kept nevertheless for perfect consistency.)\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003easrt[le,gt].d\\u003c/code\\u003e have the suffix removed.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAccording to the manual, there's no mention of operand width anywhere,\\nso remove the suffix unless more information is provided.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003e[ld,st]ptr\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003e[ld,st]ox4\\u003c/code\\u003e (Load/Store; Offset x4 or Indexed by 4).\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe instructions are created with accelerating GOT accesses in mind;\\nthey got their current semantics because the GOT is an array of pointers,\\nand pointers are at least 32-bit aligned, meaning the array offsets must be\\nat least multiples of 4.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eHowever, the operation \\u003ccode\\u003erd = *(rj + imm \\u0026lt;\\u0026lt; 2)\\u003c/code\\u003e itself is completely generic,\\nand has nothing to do with pointers. So, rename the instructions to hopefully\\navoid having to include the background material (the paragraph above) to\\nevery LoongArch learner.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003eext.w.[bh]\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003esext.[bh]\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eAccording to the manual these actually sign-extend to full native width\\n(GRLEN), regardless of whether GRLEN is 32 or not. Also the previous name is\\nnot too informative either -- \\\"ext\\\" could as well be \\\"zero-extend\\\" or\\n\\\"extract\\\" too, and that's bound to confuse people.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003ebitrev\\u003c/code\\u003e instructions are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003erevbit\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eByte/halfword-unit-reversing instructions are \\u003ccode\\u003erevb\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003erevh\\u003c/code\\u003e respectively,\\nso unify the naming.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003elu32i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e \\u003ccode\\u003elu52i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003ecu32i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e \\u003ccode\\u003ecu52i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003elu12i.w\\u003c/code\\u003e empties low bits, but \\u003ccode\\u003elu32i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003elu52i.d\\u003c/code\\u003e keeps low bits. So\\nchange the \\\"load\\\" part to \\\"concatenate/connect\\\" to distinguish.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003epcaddi\\u003c/code\\u003e is renamed \\u003ccode\\u003epcaddu2i\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eIt left-shifts the immediate by 2 before adding, just like its friends\\n\\u003ccode\\u003epcaddu12i\\u003c/code\\u003e and \\u003ccode\\u003epcaddu18i\\u003c/code\\u003e, but the \\u003ccode\\u003eu2\\u003c/code\\u003e part is curiously missing. Fix the\\ninconsistency.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003ealsl.*\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003esladd.*\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eIt's not clear what full name \\\"alsl\\\" actually stands for, so rename to\\nreflect the semantics -- \\\"Shift-Left/ScaLed Add\\\".\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003ebytepick.*\\u003c/code\\u003e are renamed \\u003ccode\\u003ecatpick.*\\u003c/code\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe original names give a false impression of somehow returning or operating\\non a single byte, while in fact it was only \\u003cem\\u003ebyte\\u003c/em\\u003e-indexed. Real operation is\\nmore like first \\u003cem\\u003econcatenating\\u003c/em\\u003e two suffix-sized values then \\u003cem\\u003epicking\\u003c/em\\u003e one\\nsuffix-sized value out from middle. Besides, cats inside the manuals are\\ncertainly nice...\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv class=\\\"markdown-heading\\\" dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\u003ch2 tabindex=\\\"-1\\\" class=\\\"heading-element\\\" dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eInstruction format notation used in this repo\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\u003ca id=\\\"user-content-instruction-format-notation-used-in-this-repo\\\" class=\\\"anchor\\\" aria-label=\\\"Permalink: Instruction format notation used in this repo\\\" href=\\\"#instruction-format-notation-used-in-this-repo\\\"\\u003e\\u003csvg data-component=\\\"Octicon\\\" class=\\\"octicon octicon-link\\\" viewBox=\\\"0 0 16 16\\\" version=\\\"1.1\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" aria-hidden=\\\"true\\\"\\u003e\\u003cpath d=\\\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\\\"\\u003e\\u003c/path\\u003e\\u003c/svg\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThe instruction format notation used in the official documentation has several\\nshortcomings that make it difficult for downstream to consume as is:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cul dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eMany format names start with a number, like \\u003ccode\\u003e2RI16\\u003c/code\\u003e, making them unsuitable as\\nidentifiers in most programming languages;\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eVariants to these \\\"base\\\" formats are not explicitly documented, forcing\\ndownstream to come up with ad-hoc names themselves;\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eExact encodings of instructions can differ even with identical assembly syntax,\\nmaking the original notation ambiguous to use.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eFor example, while \\u003ccode\\u003easrtle\\u003c/code\\u003e takes two register operands, they are not the\\nusual \\u003ccode\\u003erd, rj\\u003c/code\\u003e but \\u003ccode\\u003erj, rk\\u003c/code\\u003e. Is this \\u003ccode\\u003e2R\\u003c/code\\u003e, variant of \\u003ccode\\u003e2R\\u003c/code\\u003e or a special case\\nof \\u003ccode\\u003e3R\\u003c/code\\u003e?\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eDue to these reasons, we use a new notation for describing the various LoongArch\\ninstruction formats. The syntax is described in \\u003ca href=\\\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augmented_Backus%E2%80%93Naur_form\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\\u003eABNF\\u003c/a\\u003e as follows:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv class=\\\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\\\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\\\"insn-format  =  \\u0026quot;EMPTY\\u0026quot;\\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots\\ninsn-format  =/ imm-slots\\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots imm-slots\\n\\nreg-slots    = 1*reg\\nreg          = int-reg / fp-reg / fcc-reg / scratch-reg / lsx-reg / lasx-reg\\nint-reg      = \\u0026quot;D\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;J\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;K\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;A\\u0026quot;\\nfp-reg       = \\u0026quot;F\\u0026quot; index\\nfcc-reg      = \\u0026quot;C\\u0026quot; index\\nscratch-reg  = \\u0026quot;T\\u0026quot; index\\nlsx-reg      = \\u0026quot;V\\u0026quot; index\\nlasx-reg     = \\u0026quot;X\\u0026quot; index\\n\\nindex-length = index length\\nindex        = \\u0026quot;d\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;j\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;k\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;a\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;m\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;n\\u0026quot;\\nlength       = 1*DIGIT\\n\\nimm-slots    = 1*imm\\nimm          = signedness 1*index-length\\nsignedness   = \\u0026quot;S\\u0026quot; / 1*manual-arg\\n\\nmanual-arg   =  reg / manual-imm\\nmanual-imm   =  imm\\nmanual-imm   =/ imm postproc\\n\\npostproc     = \\u0026quot;p\\u0026quot; pp-frag\\npp-frag      = pp-op 1*DIGIT\\npp-op        = \\u0026quot;p\\u0026quot; / \\u0026quot;s\\u0026quot;\\\"\\u003e\\u003cpre class=\\\"notranslate\\\"\\u003e\\u003ccode\\u003einsn-format  =  \\\"EMPTY\\\"\\ninsn-format  =/ \\\"X\\\" index\\n\\nindex-length = index length\\nindex        = \\\"d\\\" / \\\"j\\\" / \\\"k\\\" / \\\"a\\\" / \\\"m\\\" / \\\"n\\\"\\nlength       = 1*DIGIT\\n\\nimm-slots    = 1*imm\\nimm \\\"p\\\" / \\\"s\\\"\\n\\u003c/code\\u003e\\u003c/pre\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cp dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003eThis notation has the following advantages:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cul dir=\\\"auto\\\"\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eOne name exactly specifies one encoding;\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eAll names are valid for use as identifiers in programming languages;\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eUnambiguous to parse even when capitalized;\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eProperly distinguishes between superficially similar encodings due to style=\"anchor-name: --anchored-overlay-anchor-_R_3r8ql3al1dH1_;\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" class=\"octicon octicon-list-unordered\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 0 0 1 0 2Z\"></path></svg></button></div><div class=\"js-snippet-clipboard-copy-unpositioned DirectoryRichtextContent-module__SharedMarkdownContent__hHXUL\" data-hpc=\"true\" containertiming=\"hpc\"><article class=\"markdown-body entry-content container-lg\" itemprop=\"text\"><div class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"><h1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\">List of LoongArch instructions</h1><a id=\"user-content-list-of-loongarch-instructions\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: List of LoongArch instructions\" href=\"#list-of-loongarch-instructions\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"><path d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"></path></svg></a></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">This is unofficial compiled list of currently known LoongArch instructions.\nInstruction name and encoding are taken from published instruction set manual\nfrom Loongson, then slightly modified to fix some perceived inconsistencies.</p>\n<div class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"><h2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\">License</h2><a id=\"user-content-license\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: License\" href=\"#license\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"><path d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"></path></svg></a></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Copyright © 2021-2023 Contributors to this project. All rights reserved.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The instruction encoding data tables are licensed under either <a href=\"https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/\" rel=\"nofollow\">CC-BY 4.0 International</a>\nor <a href=\"https://license.coscl.org.cn/MulanOWLBYv1\" rel=\"nofollow\">木兰开放作品许可协议 署名，第 1 版 (Mulan Open Works License Attribution, Version 1)</a>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The accompanying programs and supporting code are licensed under either\n<a href=\"https://spdx.org/licenses/Apache-2.0.html\" rel=\"nofollow\">Apache License 2.0</a>, <a href=\"https://spdx.org/licenses/MIT.html\" rel=\"nofollow\">MIT</a>\nor <a href=\"https://license.coscl.org.cn/MulanPSL2\" rel=\"nofollow\">木兰宽松许可证，第 2 版 (Mulan Permissive Software License, Version 2)</a>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The license texts are also vendored in the repo:</p>\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li><a href=\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.Apache-2.0\">LICENSE.Apache-2.0</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.CC-BY-4.0\">LICENSE.CC-BY-4.0</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MIT\">LICENSE.MIT</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MulanOWL-BY-1.0\">LICENSE.MulanOWL-BY-1.0</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"/loongson-community/loongarch-opcodes/blob/develop/LICENSE.MulanPSL-2.0\">LICENSE.MulanPSL-2.0</a></li>\n</ul>\n<details>\n<summary>Reasoning behind the licensing decisions</summary>\n<p dir=\"auto\">NOTE: The author is not a lawyer, so take the analysis below with extra\ncaution. The author believes much of the reasoning are correct however...</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The official LoongArch manuals are released by Loongson with all rights\nreserved. So first of all, we believe <em>this project is a fair use of the\noriginal work</em> because:</p>\n<ol dir=\"auto\">\n<li>The data collected here is consistent with the reality, with all original\ncontent clearly marked and explained. Hence the data tables as a whole\npose no risk to compatibility across the ecosystem, and by extension,\nLoongson's legal interests.</li>\n<li>We, and likely any potential consumer of the project, work on and/or use\nproject for personal and/or academic purposes.</li>\n<li>And even if the project is eventually being consumed for commercial uses,\nno Loongson interest is damaged because of (1).</li>\n<li>There is not any alternative that we know of, that is simultaneously:\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li>not being tied to any specific project (see below), and</li>\n<li>easy for machine consumption (the official manual is in PDF only, and\nthe English translation is in AsciiDoc).</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ol>\n<p dir=\"auto\">There are already several LoongArch instruction encoding tables in existence:</p>\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li>the array defined in <code>opcodes/loongarch-opc.c</code> of Binutils,</li>\n<li>the TableGen data files in LLVM,</li>\n<li>the <code>decodetree</code> definitions in QEMU, and</li>\n<li>other ad-hoc definitions in various adapted JIT projects.</li>\n</ul>\n<p dir=\"auto\">They are invariably hard to integrate in projects other the originating one,\nso if one wants proper LoongArch machine code support in another project they\nhappen to work on, they would have to either duplicate efforts or leverage\nthe <code>loongarch-opcodes</code> project -- compared to just giving up and adding no\nLoongArch support, existence of the <code>loongarch-opcodes</code> project actually\n<em>benefits</em> Loongson.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Regarding the copyright holder of the project, it's the contributor to this\nproject, because of <a href=\"https://www.gov.cn/guoqing/2021-10/29/content_5647633.htm\" rel=\"nofollow\">《中华人民共和国著作权法》</a>第十三条、第十四条;\nthe Chinese copyright law applies because right now all contributors to\nthe project are PRC citizens to our knowledge.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">As to why attribution is required for the data tables, instead of simply\nbeing public domain: according to 《中华人民共和国著作权法》第十条,\nthe right of attribution (署名权) is a moral right that cannot be waived.\nSo even if <a href=\"https://creativecommons.org/publicdomain/zero/1.0/\" rel=\"nofollow\">CC0-1.0</a> is\napplied to the project, in effect it would largely just become CC-BY, and\nwith the disadvantage of being harder for people to understand because the\n\"fallback path\" in the license text must be taken.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">As to why the Mulan licenses are allowed as alternative license choices:\nthis is because the author wanted to be extra safe regarding the licensing,\nespecially in the PRC jurisdiction. After checking the Chinese and English\ntexts of the Mulan licenses, the author decided there is little risk adding\nthem to the multiple-licensing choices.</p>\n</details>\n<div class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"><h2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\">Modifications to upstream specs</h2><a id=\"user-content-modifications-to-upstream-specs\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Modifications to upstream specs\" href=\"#modifications-to-upstream-specs\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"><path d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"></path></svg></a></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Some instruction mnemonics are changed, some syntactic sugar are dropped:</p>\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>dbcl</code> is renamed to <code>dbgcall</code>, and <code>hvcl</code> to <code>hypcall</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The reason why the shorter names are chosen is unclear, but <code>syscall</code> remains\nunchanged so the change actually made the naming inconsistent.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>b[lt,ge][u]</code> are renamed to <code>b[gt,le][u]</code> with corresponding operand order swapped.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">All other two-register instructions have the operand in <code>rd, rj</code> order, except\nthese jump instructions. To preserve semantics the names have to be tweaked\naccordingly. Also all other instructions with comparison semantics adopt the\n<code>gt/le</code> distinction, such as the boundary checks, so <code>lt/ge</code> is not consistent\neither.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>ertn</code> is renamed to <code>eret</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Not using <code>ret</code> for \"return\" is hard to understand, personally I think it's\nbetter to stick with widely accepted naming conventions.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>invtlb</code> is renamed to <code>tlbinv</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">All TLB manipulation instructions start with <code>tlb</code> except this one.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>csrrd</code>, <code>csrwr</code>, <code>gcsrrd</code> and <code>gcsrwr</code> are removed.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The <code>csrrd</code> and <code>csrwr</code> instructions can, to some degree, be seen as special\ncases or \"specializations\" of <code>csrxchg</code>, so remove these in favor of\nnon-overlapping encodings. <code>gcsrrd</code> and <code>gcsrwr</code> are similar.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The FCSR operands of<code>movfcsr2gr</code> and <code>movgr2fcsr</code> are marked unsigned\nimmediates instead of registers; the mnemonics are renamed to <code>fcsrrd</code> and\n<code>fcsrwr</code> as well.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The FCSR is more like a configuration word than real register in terms of\nexpected usage; but the manual and vendor toolchain all treat the slot as\nan integer register, which is obviously wrong. Instruction naming is\nadjusted accordingly (to make the FCSR more resemble CSR).</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Instructions that operate on FCCs have the <code>cf</code> part renamed to <code>fcc</code> in\ntheir mnemonics.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Other parts of the manual, especially the register names, refer to the bank\nof 1-bit FP predicates as <code>fcc</code>, but mnemonics have <code>cf</code>, which is\ninconsistent.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Naming symmetry is restored for several LBT instructions.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The x86 and ARM translation assists are almost always named <code>x86foo</code> and\n<code>armfoo</code> respectively, but annoyingly some are named <code>setx86foo</code> and\n<code>setarmfoo</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">(After <a href=\"https://sourceware.org/pipermail/binutils/2023-June/128100.html\" rel=\"nofollow\">the issue was reported</a>\nI received private confirmation that the names will not be amended but no\njustification was given; I suppose it was because the <code>set{x86,arm}foo</code> ops\nare not touching the actual LBT \"arch\" state, but I'm not sure, and here the\nadjusted names are kept nevertheless for perfect consistency.)</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>asrt[le,gt].d</code> have the suffix removed.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">According to the manual, there's no mention of operand width anywhere,\nso remove the suffix unless more information is provided.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>[ld,st]ptr</code> are renamed <code>[ld,st]ox4</code> (Load/Store; Offset x4 or Indexed by 4).</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The instructions are created with accelerating GOT accesses in mind;\nthey got their current semantics because the GOT is an array of pointers,\nand pointers are at least 32-bit aligned, meaning the array offsets must be\nat least multiples of 4.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">However, the operation <code>rd = *(rj + imm &lt;&lt; 2)</code> itself is completely generic,\nand has nothing to do with pointers. So, rename the instructions to hopefully\navoid having to include the background material (the paragraph above) to\nevery LoongArch learner.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>ext.w.[bh]</code> are renamed <code>sext.[bh]</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">According to the manual these actually sign-extend to full native width\n(GRLEN), regardless of whether GRLEN is 32 or not. Also the previous name is\nnot too informative either -- \"ext\" could as well be \"zero-extend\" or\n\"extract\" too, and that's bound to confuse people.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>bitrev</code> instructions are renamed <code>revbit</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Byte/halfword-unit-reversing instructions are <code>revb</code> and <code>revh</code> respectively,\nso unify the naming.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>lu32i.d</code> <code>lu52i.d</code> are renamed <code>cu32i.d</code> <code>cu52i.d</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>lu12i.w</code> empties low bits, but <code>lu32i.d</code> and <code>lu52i.d</code> keeps low bits. So\nchange the \"load\" part to \"concatenate/connect\" to distinguish.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>pcaddi</code> is renamed <code>pcaddu2i</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">It left-shifts the immediate by 2 before adding, just like its friends\n<code>pcaddu12i</code> and <code>pcaddu18i</code>, but the <code>u2</code> part is curiously missing. Fix the\ninconsistency.</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>alsl.*</code> are renamed <code>sladd.*</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">It's not clear what full name \"alsl\" actually stands for, so rename to\nreflect the semantics -- \"Shift-Left/ScaLed Add\".</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\"><code>bytepick.*</code> are renamed <code>catpick.*</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The original names give a false impression of somehow returning or operating\non a single byte, while in fact it was only <em>byte</em>-indexed. Real operation is\nmore like first <em>concatenating</em> two suffix-sized values then <em>picking</em> one\nsuffix-sized value out from middle. Besides, cats inside the manuals are\ncertainly nice...</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<div class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"><h2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\">Instruction format notation used in this repo</h2><a id=\"user-content-instruction-format-notation-used-in-this-repo\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Instruction format notation used in this repo\" href=\"#instruction-format-notation-used-in-this-repo\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"><path d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"></path></svg></a></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The instruction format notation used in the official documentation has several\nshortcomings that make it difficult for downstream to consume as is:</p>\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Many format names start with a number, like <code>2RI16</code>, making them unsuitable as\nidentifiers in most programming languages;</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Variants to these \"base\" formats are not explicitly documented, forcing\ndownstream to come up with ad-hoc names themselves;</p>\n</li>\n<li>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Exact encodings of instructions can differ even with identical assembly syntax,\nmaking the original notation ambiguous to use.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">For example, while <code>asrtle</code> takes two register operands, they are not the\nusual <code>rd, rj</code> but <code>rj, rk</code>. Is this <code>2R</code>, variant of <code>2R</code> or a special case\nof <code>3R</code>?</p>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Due to these reasons, we use a new notation for describing the various LoongArch\ninstruction formats. The syntax is described in <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augmented_Backus%E2%80%93Naur_form\" rel=\"nofollow\">ABNF</a> as follows:</p>\n<div class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\"><pre class=\"notranslate\"><code>insn-format  =  \"EMPTY\"\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots\ninsn-format  =/ imm-slots\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots imm-slots\n\nreg-slots    = 1*reg\nreg          = int-reg / fp-reg / fcc-reg / scratch-reg / lsx-reg / lasx-reg\nint-reg      = \"D\" / \"J\" / \"K\" / \"A\"\nfp-reg       = \"F\" index\nfcc-reg      = \"C\" index\nscratch-reg  = \"T\" index\nlsx-reg      = \"V\" index\nlasx-reg     = \"X\" index\n\nindex-length = index length\nindex        = \"d\" / \"j\" / \"k\" / \"a\" / \"m\" / \"n\"\nlength       = 1*DIGIT\n\nimm-slots    = 1*imm\nimm          = signedness 1*index-length\nsignedness   = \"S\" / \"U\"\n\n// extensions to the above, for expressing the \"manual syntax\"\nmanual-insn-format =  \"EMPTY\"\nmanual-insn-format =/ 1*manual-arg\n\nmanual-arg   =  reg / manual-imm\nmanual-imm   =  imm\nmanual-imm   =/ imm postproc\n\npostproc     = \"p\" pp-frag\npp-frag      = pp-op 1*DIGIT\npp-op        = \"p\" / \"s\"\n</code></pre><div class=\"zeroclipboard-container\">\n    <clipboard-copy aria-label=\"Copy code to clipboard\" class=\"ClipboardButton btn btn-invisible js-clipboard-copy m-2 p-0 d-flex flex-justify-center flex-items-center\" data-copy-feedback=\"Copied!\" data-tooltip-direction=\"w\" value=\"insn-format  =  &quot;EMPTY&quot;\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots\ninsn-format  =/ imm-slots\ninsn-format  =/ reg-slots imm-slots\n\nreg-slots    = 1*reg\nreg          = int-reg / fp-reg / fcc-reg / scratch-reg / lsx-reg / lasx-reg\nint-reg      = &quot;D&quot; / &quot;J&quot; / &quot;K&quot; / &quot;A&quot;\nfp-reg       = &quot;F&quot; index\nfcc-reg      = &quot;C&quot; index\nscratch-reg  = &quot;T&quot; index\nlsx-reg      = &quot;V&quot; index\nlasx-reg     = &quot;X&quot; index\n\nindex-length = index length\nindex        = &quot;d&quot; / &quot;j&quot; / &quot;k&quot; / &quot;a&quot; / &quot;m&quot; / &quot;n&quot;\nlength       = 1*DIGIT\n\nimm-slots    = 1*imm\nimm          = signedness 1*index-length\nsignedness   = &quot;S&quot; / &quot;U&quot;\n\n// extensions to the above, for expressing the &quot;manual syntax&quot;\nmanual-insn-format =  &quot;EMPTY&quot;\nmanual-insn-format =/ 1*manual-arg\n\nmanual-arg   =  reg / manual-imm\nmanual-imm   =  imm\nmanual-imm   =/ imm postproc\n\npostproc     = &quot;p&quot; pp-frag\npp-frag      = pp-op 1*DIGIT\npp-op        = &quot;p&quot; / &quot;s&quot;\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\">\n      <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" data-component=\"Octicon\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" data-view-component=\"true\" class=\"octicon octicon-copy js-clipboard-copy-icon\">\n    <path d=\"M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z\"></path><path d=\"M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z\"></path>\n</svg>\n      <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" data-component=\"Octicon\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" data-view-component=\"true\" class=\"octicon octicon-check js-clipboard-check-icon color-fg-success d-none\">\n    <path d=\"M13.78 4.22a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.06l-7.25 7.25a.75.75 0 0 1-1.06 0L2.22 9.28a.751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018L6 10.94l6.72-6.72a.75.75 0 0 1 1.06 0Z\"></path>\n</svg>\n    </clipboard-copy>\n  </div></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">This notation has the following advantages:</p>\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li>One name exactly specifies one encoding;</li>\n<li>All names are valid for use as identifiers in programming languages;</li>\n<li>Unambiguous to parse even when capitalized;</li>\n<li>Properly distinguishes between superficially similar encodings due to design\nwarts, for example:\n<ul dir=\"auto\">\n<li><code>DJ</code>, <code>JK</code>, <code>FdJ</code> and <code>DFj</code> (presumably all <code>2R</code> in official notation), or</li>\n<li><code>DSj20</code> and <code>JSd5k16</code> which are totally different formats, but nearly the\nsame in official notation (non-existent <code>1RI20</code> and base format <code>1RI21</code>).</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The field offsets and sizes for the register operand slots are as follows:</p>\n<markdown-accessiblity-table data-catalyst=\"\"><table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>Register slot</th>\n<th>Starting bit index</th>\n<th>Field size in bits</th>\n<th>Bank</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><code>D</code></td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Integer</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>J</code></td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Integer</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>K</code></td>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Integer</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>A</code></td>\n<td>15</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Integer</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>C</code></td>\n<td>Specified by the index character</td>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>FP condition code</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>F</code></td>\n<td>Specified by the index character</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>FP</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>T</code></td>\n<td>Specified by the index character</td>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>LBT scratch</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>V</code></td>\n<td>Specified by the index character</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>LSX / 128-bit SIMD</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>X</code></td>\n<td>Specified by the index character</td>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>LASX / 256-bit SIMD</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The bit index specifiers are as follows:</p>\n<markdown-accessiblity-table data-catalyst=\"\"><table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>Character</th>\n<th>Starting bit index</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><code>d</code></td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>j</code></td>\n<td>5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>k</code></td>\n<td>10</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>a</code></td>\n<td>15</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>m</code></td>\n<td>16</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>n</code></td>\n<td>18</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>\n<p dir=\"auto\">In some formats, a long immediate is broken into multiple fields. The individual\nfields are to be concatenated from left (MSB direction) to right (LSB direction)\nto form the effective number.\nFor example, the format officially known as <code>1RI21</code> is <code>JSd5k16</code> in our\nnotation; the <code>Sd5k16</code> part means <code>(int32_t)(((x &amp; 0x1f) &lt;&lt; 16) | ((x &gt;&gt; 10) &amp; 0xffff))</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The format that takes no operands is specially named <code>EMPTY</code>.\nFor all other formats, the operand slots are sorted so that all registers\nprecede the immediates, and from LSB to MSB in either group.\nThis means even instructions taking <code>rj, rd</code> as presented in official manuals\nare <code>DJ</code> format, and that <code>bstrpick.d</code> is <code>DJUk6Um6</code> and never something like\n<code>DJUm6Uk6</code> or <code>JDUk6Um6</code>.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">Because index characters can only follow certain leading characters, the whole\ninstruction format string can be capitalized without becoming ambiguous, despite\nthe index specifiers sharing the same <code>djka</code> characters with register operands.\nSo for example the <code>JSd5k16</code> name above can easily be capitalized into <code>JSD5K16</code>\nfor adherence to certain coding styles.</p>\n<div class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"><h2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\">Original format or \"Manual syntax\" of instructions</h2><a id=\"user-content-original-format-or-manual-syntax-of-instructions\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Original format or &quot;Manual syntax&quot; of instructions\" href=\"#original-format-or-manual-syntax-of-instructions\"><svg data-component=\"Octicon\" class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"><path d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"></path></svg></a></div>\n<p dir=\"auto\">In the original LoongArch ISA manual, many instructions' asm syntax is not\nconsistent with the above canonicalized notation, but instead are more-or-less\narbitrary (like with the conditional branches, no reason whatsoever for swapping\n<code>rd</code> and <code>rj</code>), and/or seem to abandon consistency for arguably ergonomics\npurposes, most commonly by hiding a shifted immediate operand's such nature,\nbut there are more.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">These original formats are recorded in the optional attribute <code>orig_fmt</code>,\nand they conform to the <code>manual-insn-format</code> ABNF item described above instead.\nMost notably, this means register operands no longer always come first, hence\nthe case-insensitive property is lost for some of the formats; also immediates\nmay optionally have to be \"postprocessed\" for proper disassembly output (or\n\"preprocessed\" for assembly), they are marked with a <code>p</code> followed by one\npostprocess operation.</p>\n<p dir=\"auto\">The possible immediate postprocess operations are listed below:</p>\n<markdown-accessiblity-table data-catalyst=\"\"><table>\n<thead>\n<tr>\n<th>Notation</th>\n<th>Meaning</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><code>pNN</code></td>\n<td><code>imm + NN</code></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><code>sNN</code></td>\n<td><code>imm &lt;&lt; NN</code></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>\n</article></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class=\"prc-PageLayout-PaneWrapper-pHPop pr-2\" style=\"--offset-header:0px;--spacing-row:var(--spacing-none);--spacing-column:var(--spacing-none)\" data-is-hidden=\"false\" data-position=\"end\"><div class=\"prc-PageLayout-HorizontalDivider-JLVqp prc-PageLayout-PaneHorizontalDivider-9tbnE\" data-variant-narrow=\"none\" data-variant-regular=\"none\" data-position=\"end\" style=\"--spacing-divider:var(--spacing-none);--spacing:var(--spacing-none)\"></div><div class=\"prc-PageLayout-Pane-AyzHK\" style=\"--spacing:var(--spacing-normal);--pane-min-width:256px;--pane-max-width:calc(100vw - var(--pane-max-width-diff));--pane-width-size:var(--pane-width-large);--pane-width:320px\"><rails-partial data-partial-name=\"codeViewRepoRoute.Sidebar\" class=\"RailsPartial-module__d-contents__G5m4w\">\n\n<div class=\"BorderGrid \">\n  <div class=\"BorderGrid-row\">\n    <div class=\"BorderGrid-cell\">\n      <div class=\"hide-sm hide-md\">\n  <h2 class=\"tmp-mb-3 h4\">About</h2>\n\n      <p class=\"f4 tmp-my-3\">\n        LoongArch Opcodes (unofficially compiled list)\n      </p>\n\n\n    <h3 class=\"sr-only\">Resources</h3>\n    <div class=\"mt-2\">\n      <a class=\"Link--muted\" data-analytics-event=\"{&quot;category&quot;:&quot;Repository data-component=\"Octicon\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" data-view-component=\"true\" class=\"octicon octicon-book mr-2 tmp-mr-2\">\n    <path d=\"M0 1.75A.75.75 0 0
